Nuruzzaman, <span style="color: black;">j:</span></span></u></strong> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; color: black;">Both the Civil Appeals, by leave, are directed against the judgment and order dated 04.08.2011 passed by the High Court Division in Writ Petition Nos. 5329 of 2006 and 2516 of 2011 making the Rules Nisi absolute and declared the judgment and order dated 3.5.2006 passed by the First Court of Settlement, Dhaka in Case No. 83 of 2003 to have been passed without lawful authority and is of no legal effect.</span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Both the civil appeals are heard together as both the writs were arose out of the same property. Those were disposed of by the High Court Division by the single judgment. They are dealt with by this single judgment. </span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Facts leading, to filing of both the civil appeals, in short, are that: </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">         </span>The present respondent No.1 in both the civil appeals as t</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; color: black;">he writ petitioners preferred the Writ Petition Nos.5329 of 2006 and 2516 of 2011 before the High Court Division challenging the judgment and order dated 03.05.2006 passed by the First Court of Settlement, Dhaka in Case No.83 of 2003 (Anx.5/02)(Ka-43 House No.3, Lane-11, Block-C, Section-10, Mirpur, Dhaka) allowing the case with direction to exclude the property in House No.3, Lane-11, Block-C, Section-10, Mirpur, Dhaka from the list of abandoned buildings stating that the land measuring 131 square yards (1 and </span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span>3/4<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">kathas) of House No.3, Lane-11, Block-C, Section-10, Mirpur, Dhaka was allotted/leased out on 21.10.1963 by Mirpur Housing Estate, Dhaka as lessor in favour of Noor Mohammad, displaced person from India, and accordingly possession of the said land was handed over to him. After taking over possession of the said land, the said Noor Mohammad had been possessing the same by erecting dwelling house and started living therein; during Liberation War, the said Noor Mohammad along with his family left the said house and after liberation he did not come back to the said house and, as such, Government took over possession the same as abandoned property. Thereafter, Mr. Ataharul Hoque, the writ petitioner of the Writ Petition No.5329 of 2006 entered into possession of the said house on 01.05.1972 and started to live therein with his family. He by dint of possession filed an application to the concerned authority for allotting the said House No.3, Lane-11, Block-C, Section-10, Mirpur Housing Estate, Dhaka in his favour. On the basis of the said application the writ respondent No.2 of the Writ Petition No.5329 of 2006 issued a Demand Note on 18.01.1975 upon the applicant with a direction to deposit arrear rent from 01.05.1972 to 31.12.1975 at the rate of Tk.85/- per month amounting to Tk.2,720/- within 23.01.1975. As per direction of the writ respondent No.2 the writ petitioner deposited the said amount of Tk.2,720/- through Challan No.H/47 dated 23.01.1975 as arrear monthly rent of the said house and on the same date it was duly informed to the Executive Engineer, Housing Settlement, Mirpur Division, Segun Bagicha, Dhaka and on 29.01.1975 the same was also duly informed to the office of the<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Administrative Officer, Mohammadpur and Mirpur Housing Estate Area. Subsequently, the writ petitioner on 03.10.1982 deposited an amount of Tk.510/through Bangladesh Bank Chalan No.Uma/10 and on 29.04.1985 also deposited an amount of Tk.13,134.40 through Bangladesh Bank Chalan No.Jha-3/4 as rents for the said abandoned property. In this way the writ petitioner deposited total amount of Tk.16,364.40 as rents of the said house. Since the original allottee of the property in question had been untraceable and the property in question was uncared in 1972, the property was declared by the Government as abandoned property and it took over the possession in the property as abandoned. The writ petitioner of Writ Petition No.5329 of 2006 has been possessing the same as tenant under the Government since 1972. The Government included the said abandoned Building in the ‘Ka’ list of the Abandoned Buildings at Serial No.43 published in Gazette Notification dated 23.09.1986 at page No.9762 (58). In the meantime, the writ respondent No.2 of Writ Petition No.5329 of 2006 vide Memorandum No.</span><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: AdarshaLipiNormal; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">n¡M¡-7/H¢f</span></strong><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: MoinaNormal; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">-85/84/480</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> dated 25.03.1985 issued a letter offering to sell the property in favour of the writ petitioner. As per condition Nos.1, 2 and 3 of the said offer letter the writ petitioner on 17.11.1985 deposited the 1<sup>st</sup> installment of an amount of Tk.23,465.20 as 20% of the total consideration amounting to Tk.1,17,326/- and also submitted an affidavit on 29.10.1985 and certificate with regard to full payment of rent of the property in question obtained from appropriate authority. After completion of all formalities a </span><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: AdarshaLipiNormal; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">“¢hœ²u Q¥¢š²</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: AdarshaLipiNormal; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">”</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> was executed on 09.10.1986 between the writ petitioner and the Government with regard to the property in question. (as described in the schedule below.) On 28.11.1985 the Ordinance No.LIV of 1985 was promulgated and the list of abandoned properties was published on 23.09.1986 and thereafter <strong>“</strong></span><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: MoinaNormal; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">¢hœ²u Q¥¢š²</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">” was executed by the Government in favour of the writ petitioner on 09.10.1986. From the Memo No.569 dated 08.10.1988 the writ petitioner learnt that the original allottee did not deposit the total consideration amount against the property in question. The writ petitioner learnt that the writ respondent No.4, Md. Murtuza Shah filed Case No.83 of 2003 in the First Court of Settlement, Dhaka praying for exclusion of the property from the abandoned properties List. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">The writ petitioner of the instant writ petition in Settlement Case No.83 of 2003 submitted an application which pending before the First Court of Settlement, Dhaka enclosing the above mentioned documents including the Municipality Tax and other utilities bills paid by him in connection with the ownership, occupation and possession of the property in question as well as certificate issued by the Local Commissioner for addition of party. But the First Court of Settlement, Dhaka refused to accept the said application filed by the writ petitioner. During the trial of the case before the Settlement Court No.1, Dhaka P.Ws. were examined including the said Mr. Md. Murtuza Shah as P.W.1. There are serious of anomalies and contradictions in the depositions of the witnesses, which will be apparent upon perusal of the depositions. The writ respondent No.4 made some false, malafide and irrelevant statements in the applications while filed the alleged application.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The First Court of Settlement, Dhaka after hearing the parties, allowed the Case No.83 of 2003 with direction to exclude the property in question from the “Ka” list of the abandoned buildings by the judgment and order dated 03.05.2006.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">      </span><span style="color: black;"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span></span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; color: black;">Against the </span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">judgment and order dated 03.05.2006 passed by the First Court of Settlement, Dhaka,<span style="color: black;"> the </span><span style="mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">writ petitioners of Writ Petition Nos.5329 of 2006 and 2516 of 2011, finding no other alternative efficacious remedy, moved the above mentioned writ petitions and obtained the Rules Nisi.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">           </span></span></span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">The writ-respondent Nos.4 and 5 in Writ Petition No.5329 of 2006 and the writ respondent Nos.2 and 3 in Writ Petition No.2516 of 2011 contested the Rules Nisi by filing separate affidavit-in-opposition. </span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">A Division Bench of the High Court Division upon hearing the parties in both writ petitions made the Rules Nisi absolute and thereby setting aside the judgment of the Settlement Court by the impugned judgment and order dated 04.08.2011.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span></span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">The leave petitioner Nos.1 and 2 feeling aggrieved by the judgment and order dated 04.08.2011 of the High Court Division preferred the Civil Petition for Leave to Appeal Nos.2024 of 2011 and 2025 of 2011 before this Division which raise the instant appeals.</span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Mr. Abdul Matin Khasru, the learned Senior Counsel, appearing on behalf of the appellant in both the civil appeals submits that the High Court Division erred in law having failed to appreciate that the respondent No.1 (writ petitioner) being a third party had no </span><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">locus standi</span></em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"> to file the writ petition challenging the judgment and order of the Court of Settlement and, as such, the instant appeals should be allowed. He further submits that the High Court Division erred in law having failed to appreciate that the Government could not produce any evidence either documentary or oral to show that the property in question comes within the definition of “abandoned property” under Article 2 of the Bangladesh Abandoned Property (Control, Management and Disposal) Order, 1972 and, as such, the instant appeals should be allowed. He next submits that the High Court Division erred in law having failed to consider that the original allottee late Noor Mohammad (father of the appellants), filed an application to the appropriate authority with proper documents within time stipulated by law to get his property released and the Court of Settlement after meticulous assessment of materials on record passed its judgment excluding the property in question from the ‘Ka’ list of the Abandoned Buildings as per provision of l<em>a</em>w enacted under the Ordinance No.54 of 1985 and, as such, the instant appeals should be allowed. He finally submits that the High Court Division erred in law having failed to appreciate that the explanation of delay in filing the writ petition is not satisfactory and, as such, the impugned judgment is liable to be set aside and the instant appeals should be allowed.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span></span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 107%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">11.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Per contra, Mr. SK. Shaifuzzaman, the learned Deputy Attorney General appearing on behalf of the respondent No.3 in Civil Appeal No.64 of 2016 and the respondent No.1 in Civil Appeal No.65 of 2016 submits that the appellants having miserably failed to discharge the burden to prove that the property in question is not an abandoned property on or before 28.02.1972. Since onus of disproving of abandoned property is squarely lies upon them as provided in Section 5 of the Ordinance,No. LIV of 1985 and, as such, the instant appeals are liable to be dismissed. He further submits that Mr. Ataharul Haque being the Government Demand Note Holder entered into an agreement for sale on 09.10.1986 with the Government as per Sale Offer vide Memorandum No.</span><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; font-family: AdarshaLipiNormal; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">n¡M¡-7/H¢f-</span></strong><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; font-family: MoinaNormal; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">85/84/480</span></strong> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">dated 25.03.1985 and paid 1<sup>st</sup> installment of Tk. 23,465.20 as 20% of the Total consideration and as such, he had got </span><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">locus-standi</span></em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"> to file the writ petition before the High Court Division as per Section 13 of the State Agreement as “</span><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; font-family: AdarshaLipiNormal; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">13z ag¢pm h¢ZÑa pÇf¢š pÇf­LÑ i¢hoÉ­a ®L¡e j¡jm¡-®j¡LŸj¡l Eáh qC­m ®œ²a¡ ¢eS c¡¢u­aÄ Eq¡ f¢lQ¡me¡ L¢l­hez</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; font-family: AdarshaLipiNormal; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">”</span> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">and as such, the instant appeals are liable to be dismissed. </span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">He next submits that the Government has no obligation either to deny the facts alleged by the claimant or to disclose the basis of treating the property as abandoned property merely because the same is disputed by the claimant and even if, any singular failure on the part of the claimants regarding whereabouts of the Original Lessee at the relevant point of date i.e. on 28.02.1972 is fully and wholly stunning and as such, the High Court Division has rightly made the Rule absolute. Hence,</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"> the instant appeals are liable to be dismissed. He finally submits that the Government has got right to property as Lessor and the Government-writ petitioner filed the writ petition with proper explanation of delay although there is no statutory limitation to challenge the legality and propriety of the judgment passed by the Court of Settlement and the High Court Division, having assessed the evidence on record, made the Rules Nisi absolute and as such, the instant appeals are liable to be dismissed.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span></span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span></span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; color: black;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">12.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Mr. Fida M. Kamal, the learned Senior Counsel appearing on behalf of the respondent No.1 in Civil Appeal No.64 of 2016 and the respondent No.3 in Civil Appeal No.65 of 2016 </span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; color: black;">made submissions in support of the impugned judgment and order of the High Court Division.</span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">13.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">We have heard the learned Senior counsel appearing for the appellant in both the civil appeals, the learned Deputy Attorney General appearing for the respondent No.3 in Civil Appeal No.64 of 2016, the respondent No.1 in Civil Appeal No.65 of 2016, also Mr. Fida M. Kamal, the learned Senior counsel appearing for the respondent No.1 in Civil Appeal No.64 of 2016 and the respondent No.3 in Civil Appeal No.65 of 2016. Perused the impugned judgment of the High Court Division, judgment of the Court of Settlement, other connected materials available on record.</span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">14.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">In the instant appeals leave were granted to consider as to whether the High Court Division erred in failing to appreciate that respondent No.1 (Writ Petitioner) being third party had no locus standi to file the writ petition challenging the judgment and order of the First Court of Settlement, Dhaka allowing the case and directing the Government to exclude the case property from the “Ka” list of the Abandoned Buildings. </span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">15.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Secondly, as to whether the High Court Division erred in law in failing to appreciate that the Government could not produce any evidence either documentary or orally to show that the property in question comes within the definition of “Abandoned Property” under Article 2 of the Bangladesh Abandoned Property (Control, Management and Disposal) Order 1972.</span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">16.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Thirdly, as to whether the High Court Division erred in law in failing to appreciate that the explanation of delay in filing the writ petition is not satisfactory and the Court of Settlement passed the judgment and order after proper and meticulous assessment of evidence on record allowing the case and directing the Government to exclude the case property from the “Ka” list of the Abandoned Buildings.</span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">17.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">As regards to the ground filing of writ petition by the third party is required to scan as to whether he has any legal right over the property in question pending settlement case between the admitted allottee owner and Government Lessor. The original allottee when questioning the vesting of property, as per section 7 of the said ordinance as to the abandoned property and listing the same in “Ka” list, before the competent Settlement Court to decide the propriety of vesting, there is no reason and scope to resolve any claim made by the third party through Government vide a contract of purchase. Because, the provision of ordinance provides no room to resolve any claim of right and title of contracting party by the Court of Settlement. The Court of settlement only can see as per application under section 7 of the ordinance, as to whether the case property is abandoned or not.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">     </span></span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 107%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">18.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">The High Court Division in the judgment has already noticed that the respondent No.1-Ataharul Haque had applied to be added as a party in the settlement case before the Court of Settlement which was refused. The respondent No.1 did not challenge the order of refusal, nevertheless, after passing the judgment by the Settlement Court excluding the property from the “Ka” list of the Abandoned Buildings filed <span style="letter-spacing: -.2pt;">the writ petition challenging the aforementioned</span> excluding before the High Court Division. In the above facts and circumstances, this Division is of the firmed view that writ petition by the third party could not be maintainable, rather, it is quite superfluous. In this regard we can safely held that before issuing the Rule the High Court Division ought to have gone through the merit of the Writ Petition and if it is apparent from the statement of the Writ Petition that the Petitioner neither aggrieved person nor have any locus standi to file the <span style="letter-spacing: -.2pt;">Writ Petition, such type of Vexatious application</span> should be rejected summarily .The Writ Petitioner of the Writ Petition No.5329 of 2006 has got no personal interest in the case property either as tenant or so called purchaser.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>His claim must be governed according to the result of his landlord vendor’s case. It is, therefore, our considered view that the High Court Division appears to have misconstrued and misconceived their jurisdiction under article 102 in holding that the Writ Petition is maintainable.</span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">19.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">As regards to the second ground whether as per definition of “Abandoned Property” under Article 2 of the Bangladesh Abandoned Property (Control, Management and Disposal) Order 1972, the property in question comes within that purview. The concept of abandoned property, according to article No.2(1) of President Order No.16 of 1972 runs as follows: </span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Defining part</span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="margin-left: .75in; text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level3 lfo1;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(1)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">“abandoned property” means any property owned by any person who is not present in Bangladesh or whose whereabouts are not known or who has ceased to occupy supervise or manage in person his property, including –</span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Inclusion clauses</span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="margin-left: .75in; text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo2;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(i)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">     </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">any property owned by any person who is a citizen of a State which at any time after the 25<sup>th</sup> day of March, 1971, was at war with or engaged in military<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>operation against the People’s Republic of Bangladesh;</span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="margin-left: .75in; text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo2;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(ii)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">   </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">any property taken over under the Bangladesh (Taking over of Control and Management of Industrial and Commercial Concerns) Order, 1972 (Acting President’s Order No.1 of 1972), but does not include – </span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Exclusion clauses </span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: .75in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(a)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">any property the owner of which is residing outside Bangladesh for any purpose which, in the opinion of the Government, is not prejudicial to the interest of Bangladesh;</span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: .75in; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(b)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">   </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">any property which is in the possession or under the control of the Government under any law for the time being in force.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span></span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Explanation.-“Person who is not present in Bangladesh” includes any body of persons or company constituted or incorporated in the territory or under the laws of a State which at any time after the 25<sup>th</sup> day of March, 1971, was at war with or engaged in military operations against the People’s Republic of Bangladesh.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">20.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">According to definition it appears clearly that if any person who left his property or is not present in Bangladesh or whose whereabouts are not known or who has ceased to occupy, supervise or manage in person his property, during the period of<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>liberation in 1971 was at war with or engaged in military operation against the Bangladesh, his property under the definition shall be included as an abandoned property. </span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">21.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">On a careful perusal of the judgment of the Court of Settlement it is clearly revealed that the petitioner before the Court of Settlement produced 10 (ten) prosecution witnesses and exhibited so many documents. </span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">22.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">On the other hand the respondent Government neither produced any oral or documentary evidence for rebutting the prosecution explanation offered in the oral and documentary evidences regarding Noor Mohammod’s living in Bangladesh. Rather, from the trend of the cross it reveals that they would like to establish that claimants are not the legal heirs of the late Noor Mohammod. It is must be mentioned here that Noor Mohammod had filed the application on 17-09-1986 under section 7 of the ordinance LIV of 1985, the final gazette was published on 23-9-1986 including the property as abandoned property at page no. 9762 (58) being serial No.43. In respect of the legal heirs, the petitioners before the settlement Court filed the copy of succession certificate vide Succession case No. 631 of 1996, certificate being issued by a competent<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>Court which did not revoke till today. More so, they had deposited some certificate copies of the complaint case being No. 5 of 97 of the tribunal No. 1 of Bangladesh Bar Council and copy of passport of the Noor Mohammod. Noor Mohammod died on 10.02.1987. The leave petitioners were substituted by the settlement Court as the legal heirs. The government did not challenge those events before any court.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 107%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">23.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">The Settlement Court found from the evidence on record that Noor Mohammod <span style="letter-spacing: -.2pt;">never left the Bangladesh, rather, on 04.02.1972</span> he shifted from the property in question for fear of his life to House No.7, Land No.4, Block-C, Avenuce-3, Section-11 of Mirpur, Dhaka. So, there is no question arises as to Noor Mohammod’s leaving the country. There is no iota of evidence on the side of the Government that Noor Mohammod had not shifted the house nor they had produced any oral and documentary evidences that Noor Mohammod left Bangladesh. It is further depicted from the record that Noor Mohammod could not manage or supervise the case property for a short period. The such type of absence from the case property does not take away his right and title in respect of case property as he did not left the country, rather had been trying to release the property. Therefore, the Court of Settlement rightly found that Noor Mohammod never left Bangladesh. It was also found by the Court of Settlement that Noor Mohammod had applied for passport and on 24.09.1979 a passport was issued in the name of Noor Mohammod as a <span style="letter-spacing: -.2pt;">permanent resident of Bangladesh. This passport</span> proved that Noor Mohammod was a permanent resident of Bangladesh until death and lived in Bangladesh. He died on 10.02.1987 which has been clearly mentioned in a Death Certificate issued by the Local Commissioner and certificate issued from the concerned authority of the graveyard. Therefore, the Court of Settlement believed the prosecution story thoroughly examining the oral deposition and documentary evidence. The High Court Division without controverting the aforesaid unimpeachable evidence reversed the facts of finding of the Court of Settlement, as if, it is a Court of appeal which is not only beyond the jurisdiction under article 102 of the Constitution, rather, such exercise is colourable and fenciful which is deprecated by this Division. So, the High Court Division under article 102 could not act as a Court of appeal.</span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: normal; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">24.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">This Division in the long line of catena has already held that the High Court Division only could interfere with the finding of the Court of Settlement, if could be shown that the tribunal had acted without jurisdiction or made findings upon no evidence or without considering any material evidence causing prejudice to a party or it had acted malafide or in violation of any principle of natural justice. The High Court Division has failed to appreciate any such lacking in the judgment of Settlement Court, even then, it set aside the judgment of settlement Court.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: normal; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">25.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Noor Mohammod had filed the application on 17.09.1986 to the abandoned property cell of Ministry of Works for releasing the property vide a receipt No.3712 which has ultimately given rising to Settlement Case No.83 of 2003. So, it is crystal clear that the Late Noor Mohammad had filed the application within time as per provision of Ordinance No.LIV of 1985 though the case Number was recorded in the year 2003.</span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">26.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">It is, therefore, clearly depicted that the filling of case in the Court of Settlement by the Noor Mohammod not barred by law as opined by the High Court Division.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>It is therefore obvious, the findings in the judgment of High Court Division as to non-consideration of evidence by the Settlement Court bears no significance. Ratherest, the Judgment of the High Court Division is so </span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">inappreciable</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"> which justifying calls for interference by this Division. </span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">27.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">The next ground is whether the High Court Division erred in failing to appreciate that sole respondent of the settlement case Secretary, Ministry of Housing and Public Works filed the writ petition without any delay acting with due diligence. On a careful scrutiny of the record of the Writ Petition No.2516 of 2011 it is apparent on the face of the cause title of the writ petition that the impugned judgment was passed on 03.05.2006 and an affidavit was sworn on 22<sup>nd</sup> day of March 2011; therefore, filing of the writ petition was not only delayed, ratherest, shockingly and unprecedented delay has been caused in invoking the special original jurisdiction under article 102 of the Constitution, though settlement case<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>was allowed on contest against the writ petitioner Government denying the material allegations, not only that, moreso,<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>they also cross examined all the P.Ws.</span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">28.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Now this Division will look into the behaviorally attitude regarding seeking the redress under article 102 of the Constitution.</span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">29.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Though no period of limitation has been prascribed by law for seeking redress under article 102 of the constitution. However, such relief must be sought as early as possible and must be shown due diligence. There is no special provision of privilege for the Government to explain the delay invoking constitutional jurisdiction. In the case in our hand, the Government even in the relevant paragraph of the Writ<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Petition did not explain the knowledge about the judgment, filing of application and obtaining of the certified copy, nor cause any reason in the application for what cause it has not filed the writ application as early as possible after passing the judgment.</span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">30.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">As we have already noticed the date of judgment and swearing the date of affidavit for filing the writ petition, we cannot but to opine that there is no sufficient explanation for condonation of such inordinate delay. It is therefore, well established that the respondent Government was not vigilant for the filing the writ petition, probably it has acted in persuasion of the third party who filed the writ petition in the year 2006, even then, the Government had filed the writ petition in 2011 just before hearing and judgment of the High Court Division.</span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">31.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In the facts, circumstances and instant situation of the case we cannot but to hold that </span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">inordinate delay in seeking relief can’t be justified</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> according to explanation offered to condone the delay in accordance with law. Ratherest, it is clearly justifying to interference with the judgment of the High Court Division because the High Court Division in maintaining the writ application acted beyond the settle maxim of law in regard to condonation of delay. </span></p><p class="MsoBodyText2" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">32.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Accordingly we find substance in both the appeals. The appeals are hereby allowed. The judgment of the High Curt Division is set aside.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: .5in; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Ed. </span></strong></p><div style="mso-element: footnote-list;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><!--[endif]--><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><a href="file:///H:/Issue_%20October%202019%20(2)/Issue__October_19__C.%20A.%2064-65%20of%2016__Nuruzzaman_J___AD___2.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt; color: black;">CIVIL APPEAL Nos.</span></u></strong></a><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt; color: black;"> 64-65<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>OF 2016 </span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoBodyText" style="margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 9.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">(From the judgment and order dated 04.08.2011 passed by the High Court Division in Writ Petition Nos.5329 of 2006 and 2516 of 2011)</span></p></div></div></div></div>
804	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Md. Shahjamal Sardar and others Vs.  Bangladesh and others</h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> Writ Petition No. 14344 of 2017 </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  Naima Haider, J.)</p><p><b>Court:</b> High Court Division,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. Abdullah Mahmood Hasan with Mr. Md. Hemait Ullah, Advocates ,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2019(2) LNJ  </p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2019</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Md. Shahajamal Sardar and others  </p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  Government of Bangladesh and others </p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Constitutions of Bangladesh</p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2020-03-15</p><!DOCTYPE html><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">HIGH COURT DIVISION</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">(SPECIAL ORIGINAL JURISDICTION)</span></strong></p><table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="MsoNormalTable" style="margin-left: 5.4pt; border-collapse: collapse; height: 145px;" width="593"><tbody><tr style="mso-yfti-irow: 0; mso-yfti-firstrow: yes; mso-yfti-lastrow: yes;"><td style="width: 262.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top"><p class="MsoHeading8" style="line-height: 110%; margin: 0in -1.4pt 6.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt; font-style: normal; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Naima Haider, J</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">And</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Khizir Ahmed Choudhury, J. </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-right: -1.45pt; text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Judgment on</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><a href="file:///H:/Issue_%20October%202019%20(2)/Issue%20__October__19(2)__W.%20P.%2014344%20of%2017_Naima%20Haider,%20J.__2.doc#_ftn1" name="_ftnref1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><span class="MsoFootnoteReference"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: Symbol; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;"><span style="mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;">}</span></span></span></a></p></td><td style="width: 239.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt;"><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Md. Shahajamal Sardar and others </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: right;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">. . .Petitioners</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">-Versus-</span></strong></p><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Government of Bangladesh and others </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: right;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">. . .Respondents </span></strong></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.25pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Constitutions of Bangladesh, 1972</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.25pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"> </p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Article 102</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The legislative powers shall be vested in the Parliament and notwithstanding the same, Parliament may delegate power to make orders, regulations and other instruments having legislative effect. This Division in exercise of powers under Article 102 of the Constitution can review the constitutionality of a primary legislation. If this can be done, the legality of a delegated legislation can always be subject to judicial scrutiny. <span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">      </span>Delegated legislation can be struck down if: (a) the delegated legislation is void because the delegating statute is unconstitutional, (b) the delegated legislation offends the constit-</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">utional provisions, (c) the delegated legislation</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> is ultra vires the delegating statute, or (d) the delegated legislation is arbitrary, unreasonable or contrary to any </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.4pt;">other statutory provisions. A delegated legislation</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> or any provision therein may also be struck down if it is so vague that a reasonable interpretation is not possible.  The purpose of subordinate legislation is to carry into effect the existing law and not to change it. Therefore, when Parliament delegates legislative functions to the administrative agencies to make rules or regulations, Parliament cannot be said to have permitted the delegate to make arbitrary and unreasonable rules; an unreasonable delegated legislation, in our view, does not carry into effect the parent law. While there are various tests which are applied in determining whether a delegated legislation is unreasonable, in our view, an appropriate test is <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">“whether the delegated legislation is so unreasonable that Parliament cannot be taken has having authorized it to be made under the Act in question”</em> <span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">     </span>... (10 and 11)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: TonnyBanglaMJ;">AwaMÖnYK…Z †emiKvix cÖv_wgK we`¨vjq wkÿK (PvKzix kZ©vejx wba©viY) wewagvjv, 2013</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: TonnyBanglaMJ;">wewa 2(M) Ges 9(1)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">The effect of Rule 2(Ga) is that if a teacher renders, say 10 years of service prior to nationalization, his effective service period under the 2013 shall be 50% thereof, i.e. 5 years. However, if the particular teacher’s term of service is less than 4 years, then his previous service years shall not be counted after the nationalization. The issue is whether this provision, should be struck down. The respondents did not offer any explanation on the rationale of Rule 2(Ga) of the 2013 Rules. Regardless, our understanding is as follows: the teachers who are nationalized, shall cease to be private employees and shall be treated as Government employees. They shall be entitled to different Government facilities, including but not limited to pension benefits. We are mindful of the fact that the Government has nationalized hundreds of schools and in the process, affirmed the status of the employees and teachers of those schools as Government employees entitled to pension benefits and other benefits. If Rule 2(Ga) is was drafted differently to take account of the entire period of service prior to nationalization, then it would have had </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">severe financial implications on the Government. Rule 2(Ga) of the 2013 Rules is therefore, in our view, the mechanism used to reduce the financial exposure and at the same time, provide benefits to the teachers. The learned Counsel for the petitioners submits that as a result of Rule 2(Ga) of the 2013 </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">Rules, the petitioners’ “rights and entitlements” have been affected to their</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.2pt;"> prejudice and therefore, Rule 2(Ga) should be struck down.</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.2pt;"> <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">Now, let us consider the legality of Rule 9 of the 2013 Rules. The 2013 Rules apply in respect of the teachers of the nationalized institutions. After nationalization in 2013, the teachers</strong></span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> of the newly nationalized schools were absorbed into Government service. <span style="letter-spacing: -.2pt;">The </span></span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: TonnyBanglaMJ; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">ÒKvh©Ki PvKzixKvjÓ</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.2pt;"> of the nationalized teachers would be </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: TonnyBanglaMJ; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">AwaMÖn‡Yi c~‡e© GKvw`µ‡g †h †gqv‡` PvKzix Kwiqv‡Qb Dnvi 50%.</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.2pt;"> So, if a teacher was teaching for say, 10 years, in a the school which was nationalized, his </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: TonnyBanglaMJ; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">ÒKvh©Ki PvKzixKvjÓ </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">would be deemed to be 5 years. Rule 9(1) provides that the seniority shall be counted by reference to </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: TonnyBanglaMJ; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">Kvh©KiPvKzix Kv‡ji wfwË‡Z</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: TonnyBanglaMJ; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">.<strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></strong></span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">We were informed by the learned Counsels for the respondents that after</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> <span style="letter-spacing: -.2pt;">nationalization, appointments can be made directly only. The new direct recruit would not, immediately after his appointment, have </span></span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: TonnyBanglaMJ; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">PvKzixKvj</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.2pt;"> of 5 years; the direct appointee must serve as a teacher for 5 years for him to have tenure of service of 5 years. In the meantime, the teacher who was nationalized would be working for 5 more years, as nationalized teacher and his total tenure would be 10 years. However, under Rule 9(1) of the 2013 Rules, the direct appointee shall be senior to the teacher who has been nationalized under the 2013 Rules despite the fact that his tenure</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> of service is less than the tenure of service of the nationalized teacher. This is manifestly absurd, particularly when </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">the teachers directly recruited an</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">d nationalized teachers are treated at pa</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">r.</span></strong> <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">We are dealing with the issue whether Rule 9(1) and Rule 2(Ga) of the 2013 Rules should be struck down as being unreasonable. We have concluded that Rule 9(1) of the 2013 Rules is manifestly unreasonable and self contradictory and therefore, is liable to be struck down.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">  </span>. . . (13-15 and 19)</span></strong></p><p class="Normal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;">Mr. Abdullah Mahmood Hasan with</span></p><p class="Normal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;">Mr. Md. Hemait Ullah, Advocates</span></p><p align="right" class="Normal" style="text-align: right; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;">. . . For the Petitioners</span></strong></p><p class="Normal" style="margin-left: .5in; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;">Mr. Taufiq Sajawar Partho, AAG</span></p><p align="right" class="Normal" style="text-align: right; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;">. . . For the Respondent No. 4</span></strong></p><p class="Normal" style="margin-left: .5in; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">Mr. A.K.M. Habibur Rahman, Advocate</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">. . . For the Respondent Nos. 8 &amp; 9.</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></p><p class="Normal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.35pt; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;">Naima Haider, J:</span></u></em></strong> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;">In this application under Article 102 of the Constitution, Rule Nisi was issued in the following terms: </span></p><p class="Normal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 27.35pt;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">   </span>Let a Rule Nisi be issued calling upon the respondents to show cause as to why Rule 2(Ga) of </span></em><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: MoinaNormal; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">A¢dNËqZL«a ®hplL¡l£ fÐ¡b¢jL ¢hcÉ¡mu ¢nrL (Q¡L¥l£ naÑ¡hm£ ¢ed¡ÑlZ) ¢h¢dj¡m¡, 2013</span></em></strong><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;"> deducting 50% Service Tenure of the Teachers of Registered Non Government Primary School (Now Nationalized) should not be declared to be ultra vires to the Constitution of the People’s Republic of Bangladesh and why a direction should not be given upon the respondent to consider the entire service tenure of the respective petitioner from the date of enlisting the monthly pay order as a teacher of registered Non Government Primary School (New Nationalized) and why a direction should not be given upon the respondent Nos. 1-5 to take necessary steps for ensuring salary and other service benefits to the petitioner as Headmaster of Registered Government Primary School (New Nationalized) and/ or pass such other or further order or orders as to this Court may seem fit and proper. </span></em></p><p class="Normal" style="text-align: justify;
