line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">Subsequently an Application for Addition</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;"> of Party was filed. This Division allowed the said Application and the applicants were added as co-petitioners in the proceeding before us.</span></p><p class="Normal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;">An Application for issuance of Supplementary Rule was also filed by the petitioners. The said Application was allowed and Supplementary Rule was issued in the following terms:</span></p><p class="Normal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 27.0pt;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">   </span>Let a supplementary Rule Nisi be issued calling upon the respondents to show cause as to why Rule 9 of the </span></em><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: AdarshaLipiNormal; mso-bidi-font-family: TonnyBanglaMJ;">A¢dNËqZL«a ®hplL¡l£ fÐ¡b¢jL ¢hcÉ¡mu ¢nrL (Q¡L¥l£naÑ¡¢c ¢ed¡ÑlZ) ¢h¢dj¡m¡,</span></em></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: MoinaNormal; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> 2013</span></em></strong><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;"> shall not be declared to be unlawful and unconstitutional and violative of the fundamental right guaranteed under the Constitution and why the respondents should not be directed to treat the petitioners as Head Maters of their respective school till their regular retirement age, unless otherwise disqualified and/ or pass such other or further order or orders as to this Court may seem fit and proper.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></em></p><p class="Normal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;">The relevant facts, in brief, are set out as follows: the petitioners are law abiding citizens of Bangladesh and are Head Masters of different schools. The petitioners joined their respective schools as teachers after obtaining the requisite educational qualifications. Subsequently, the petitioners had been promoted as Head Masters of their respective schools, further to the approvals of the concerned District Primary Education Officer. The petitioners have been discharging their functions to the full satisfaction of all concerned. Some of the petitioners were discharging the functions as Head Master from as early as 1990. Though the petitioners had been performing the functions as Head Master, unfortunately, the petitioners did not obtain Pay Scale relevant to the post of Head Masters. The petitioners nevertheless continued to serve as Head Masters of their respective schools. The Government decided to nationalize certain schools. All the schools in which the petitioners are Head Masters had been nationalized. The Government also framed the </span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: TonnyBanglaMJ;">AwaMÖnYK…Z †emiKvwi cÖv_wgK we`¨vj‡qi wkÿK (PvKzixkZ©vw` wba©viY) wewagvjv,</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ;"> 2013</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: Arial;"> (</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;">“the 2013 Rules”) which sets out the terms and conditions of the service of the nationalized teachers, including the petitioners. The 2013 Rules was framed by the Government without taking suggestions from the different stake holders, though such consultation process was required. When the 2013 Rules were available, it transpired that certain provisions cause extreme prejudice to the petitioners and takes away the vested rights. Being aggrieved, the petitioners moved this Division and obtained the Rule. Subsequently, the petitioners filed an Application for Issuance of Supplementary Rule and the said Application was allowed. </span></p><p class="Normal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 105%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;">The petitioners filed two separate Supplementary Affidavits, annexing certain documents to show, among others, that the process of appointment and fixation of the salary of the petitioners had completed been through the respondents.</span></p><p class="Normal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;">The Rule is opposed. The respondent No.4 filed an Affidavit in Opposition. With regard to the Rule issuing order, the respondent No.4 states that Rule 2(Ga) of the 2013 Rules is legal; the petitioners had voluntarily joined knowing that their service tenure would be reduced and therefore, the petitioners are estopped form raising this issue. Furthermore, since the 2013 Rules were framed in accordance with the procedure laid down under the Primary School (Taking Over) Act 1974, there is no scope for this Division to interfere. In the Affidavit in Opposition, it is stated that the promotion to the post of Head Master can be made if the person has the requisite qualification. Furthermore, to be eligible for promotion to the post of Head Master, the person must be working as Assistant Teacher for 7 years from the date of enlistment in the MPO. After nationalization, the Government issued an order which states that there is no scope to promote Assistant Teachers to Head Masters. Through the Affidavit, it is pointed out that the documents submitted by the petitioners are under challenge and questionable and therefore, this Division should not intervene. Through the Affidavit, the respondent No.4 also points out <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">“That the petitioners claim that they are discharging their duties and Headmaster is not true and hence denied”</em>. The respondent No.4 refers to the order passed by the Full Bench of the Hon’ble Appellate Division in Civil Petition for Leave to Appeal No. 4014 of 2018. The Full Bench of the Hon’ble Appellate Division confirmed the order of stay passed by the Hon’ble Judge in Chamber and directed disposal on merit. The learned Counsel, referring to his order of the Full Bench of the Hon’ble Appellate Division submits that the interim order passed by this Division had been stayed by the Hon’ble Judge in Chamber and this indicates that there is no merit in the Rule.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>On these, among other counts, the learned Counsel submits that the Rule and the Supplementary Rule should be discharged.</span></p><p class="Normal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;">The Rule is also opposed by the respondent Nos. 8-10. In the Affidavit in Opposition, it is stated that the 2013 Rule was framed in accordance with law and therefore, interference by this Division is not warranted. In the Affidavit in Opposition, it is stated that under the 2013 Rules, the direct appointees shall have preference over those who were nationalized and therefore, the direct appointees should be made Head Masters. It is also pointed out that on similar matters, the petitioners filed series of writ petition but there was no disclosure and therefore, the Rule and the Supplementary Rule should be discharged. Through the Affidavit in Opposition, the maintainability of the instant writ petition was also questioned. </span></p><p class="Normal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;">The learned Counsel appearing for the petitioners at the outset takes us through the 2013 Rules. He submits that if the effective service period is reduced, as has been done by Rule 2(Ga) of the 2013 Rules, the petitioners’ entitlement under the 2013 Rules would be detrimentally affected. The learned Counsel submits that delegated legislations are framed to further the objective of the parent legislation. The learned Counsel in support refers to certain decisions of the Supreme Court of India. Taking us through these decisions, the learned Counsel submits that Rule 2(Ga) of the 2013 Rules, reducing the “effective service period by half” does not have objective basis and therefore, should be struck down. The learned Counsel referring to Rule 9(1) of the 2013 Rules, submit that due to the operation of Rule 9(1), the seniority of the petitioners would be affected seriously; the petitioners would always remain junior to whoever is appointed directly. This, the learned Counsel submits, is manifestly arbitrary and absurd. Since after nationalization, there is only scope for direct recruitment, the interpretation of Rule 9(1) would be that the petitioners would never be senior to the junior most appointee. The petitioners, as Headmasters, serving for more than 20 years would remain junior to any teacher directly recruited. According to the learned Counsel, if under the 2013 Rules, the effective service is reduced to half, then the revised service period should be taken into account; if that is taken into account, Rule 9(1) of the 2013 Rules cannot stand because this has the effect of “continuous reduction of length of service”.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>According to the learned Counsel, Rule 9(1) of the 2013 Rules is manifestly unreasonable, takes away the petitioners’ vested rights and is vague; thus Rule 9(1) should be struck. The learned Counsel submits that for the reasons set out aforesaid, the Rule should be made absolute with appropriate direction upon the respondents.</span></p><p class="Normal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;">We have heard the learned Counsels at length. We have also perused the pleading and the documents annexed therein.</span></p><p class="Normal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;">Article 65 of the Constitution provides that the legislative powers shall be vested in the Parliament and notwithstanding the same, Parliament may delegate power to make orders, regulations and other instruments having legislative effect. This Division in exercise of powers under Article 102 of the Constitution can review the constitutionality of a primary legislation. If this can be done, the legality of a delegated legislation can always be subject to judicial scrutiny. This is the principle settled by the Hon’ble Appellate Division in series of cases. Delegated legislation can be struck down if: (a) the delegated legislation is void because the delegating statute is unconstitutional, (b) <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">the delegated legislation offends the constitutional</span> provisions, (c) the delegated legislation is ultra vires the delegating statute, or (d) the delegated legislation is arbitrary, unreasonable or contrary to any other statutory provisions. A delegated legislation or any provision therein may also be struck down if it is so vague that a reasonable interpretation is not possible.</span></p><p class="Normal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">11.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;">The purpose of subordinate legislation is to carry into effect the existing law and not to change it. Therefore, when Parliament delegates legislative functions to the administrative agencies to make rules or regulations, Parliament cannot be said to have permitted the delegate to make arbitrary and unreasonable rules; an unreasonable delegated legislation, in our view, does not carry into effect the parent law. While there are various tests which are applied in determining whether a delegated legislation is unreasonable, in our view, an appropriate test is <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">“whether the delegated legislation is so unreasonable that Parliament cannot be taken has having authorized it to be made under the Act in question”</em>. </span></p><p class="Normal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">12.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;">The issue before this Division is whether Rule 2(Ga) and Rule 9(1) of the 2013 Rules should be struck down. The relevant provisions are set out below for ease of reference:</span></p><p class="Normal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;">Rule 2(Ga) of the 2013 Rules </span></u></strong></p><p class="Normal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: TonnyBanglaMJ;">ÒKvh©Ki PvKzixKvjÓ A_© †Kvb wkÿK AwaMÖn‡Yi c~‡e© GKvw`µ‡g †h †gqv‡` PvKzix Kwiqv‡Qb Dnvi 50%| </span></strong></p><p class="Normal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: TonnyBanglaMJ;">Z‡e kZ© _v‡K †h, †Kvb wkÿK AwaMÖn‡Yi Ae¨ewnZ c~‡e© GKvw`µ‡g 4 (Pvi) erm‡ii Kg PvKzix Kwiqv _vwK‡j D³ PvKzixKvj wnmv‡e MY¨ nB‡e bv;</span></strong></p><p class="Normal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 27.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ;">9| </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: TonnyBanglaMJ;">wkÿK‡`i †R¨ôZv, c‡`vbœwZ, BZ¨vw`|- (1) wewa 4 Gi Aaxb †Kvb wkÿ‡Ki wb‡qvM cÖ`v‡bi ZvwiL nB‡Z Kvh©KiPvKzix Kv‡ji wfwË‡Z wkÿK c‡` Zvnvi †R¨ôZv MYbv Kiv nB‡e Ges D³ Zvwi‡Li Ae¨ewnZ c~‡e© wb‡qvMwewai Aaxb wkÿK c‡` mivmwi wb‡qvMcÖvß me©‡kl e¨w³i wb‡¤œ D³ wkÿ‡Ki Ae¯’vb wba©vwiZ nB‡e|</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 27.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: TonnyBanglaMJ;">(2) wb‡qvMcÖ`v‡bi ci wkÿKM‡Yi cvi¯úwiK †R¨ôZv Zvnv‡`i ¯^-¯^ Kvh©KiPvKzix Kv‡ji wfwË‡Z wba©viY Kwi‡Z nB‡e Ges Kvh©KiPvKzixKvj GKB ev mgvb nB‡j Zvnv‡`i b~b¨Zg wkÿvMZ †hvM¨Zv AR©‡bi erm‡ii Ges D³ ermi GKB nB‡j eq‡mi wfwË‡Z †R¨ôZv wba©vwiZ nB‡e| </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 27.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: TonnyBanglaMJ;">(3) wb‡qvM wewai kZ© c~iY mv‡c‡ÿ, Dc-wewa (1) I (2) Gi Aaxb †R¨ôZvi wfwË‡Z wkÿKMY c‡`vbœwZ, wm‡jKkb †MÖW Ges cÖ‡hvR¨ UvBg †¯‹j cÖvc¨ nB‡eb| </span></strong></p><p class="Normal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">13.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;">The effect of Rule 2(Ga) is that if a teacher renders, say 10 years of service prior to nationalization, his effective service period under the 2013 shall be 50% thereof, i.e. 5 years. However, if the particular teacher’s term of service is less than 4 years, then his previous service years shall not be counted after the nationalization. The issue is whether this provision, should be struck down.</span></p><p class="Normal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">14.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;">This provision is strange but not unreasonable. The respondents did not offer any explanation on the rationale of Rule 2(Ga) <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">of the 2013 Rules. Regardless, our understanding</span> is as follows: the teachers who are nationalized, shall cease to be private employees and shall be treated as Government employees. They shall be entitled to different Government facilities, including but not limited to pension benefits. We are mindful of the fact that the Government has nationalized hundreds of schools and in the process, affirmed the status of the employees and teachers of those schools as Government employees entitled to pension benefits and other benefits. If Rule 2(Ga) is was drafted differently to take account of the entire period of service prior to nationalization, then it would have had severe financial implications on the Government. Rule 2(Ga) of the 2013 Rules is therefore, in our view, the mechanism used to reduce the financial exposure and at the same time, provide benefits to the teachers. The learned Counsel for the petitioners submits that as a result of Rule 2(Ga) of the 2013 Rules, the petitioners’ “rights and entitlements” have been affected to their prejudice and therefore, Rule 2(Ga) should be struck down. Yes, it can be argued that the effect of Rule 2(Ga) is that the petitioners’ expectation to service benefits is <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">affected; however, expectation is not synonymous</span> to “rights and entitlement”. Loss of expectation of the petitioners cannot be a ground to strike down Rule 2(Ga) of the 2013 Rules.</span></p><p class="Normal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">15.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;">Now, let us consider the legality of Rule 9 of the 2013 Rules. The 2013 Rules apply in respect of the teachers of the nationalized institutions. After nationalization in 2013, the teachers of the newly nationalized schools were absorbed into Government service. The </span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: TonnyBanglaMJ;">ÒKvh©Ki PvKzixKvjÓ</span></strong> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;">of the nationalized teachers would be </span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: TonnyBanglaMJ;">AwaMÖn‡Yi c~‡e© GKvw`µ‡g †h †gqv‡` PvKzix Kwiqv‡Qb Dnvi 50%</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: TonnyBanglaMJ;">.</span> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;">So, if a teacher was teaching for say, 10 years, in a the school which was nationalized, his </span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: TonnyBanglaMJ;">ÒKvh©Ki PvKzixKvjÓ</span></strong> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;">would be deemed to be 5 years. Rule 9(1) provides that the seniority shall be counted by reference to </span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: TonnyBanglaMJ;">Kvh©KiPvKzix Kv‡ji wfwË‡Z</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: TonnyBanglaMJ;">.</span> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span>We were informed by the learned Counsels for the respondents that after nationalization, appointments can be made directly only. The new direct recruit would not, immediately after his appointment, have </span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: TonnyBanglaMJ;">PvKzixKvj </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;">of 5 years; the direct appointee must serve as a teacher for 5 years for him to have tenure of service of 5 years. In the meantime, the teacher who was nationalized would be working for 5 more years, as nationalized teacher and his total tenure would be 10 years. However, under Rule 9(1) of the 2013 Rules, the direct appointee shall be senior to the teacher who has been nationalized under the 2013 Rules despite the fact that his tenure of service is less than the tenure of service of the nationalized teacher. This is manifestly absurd, particularly when the teachers directly recruited and nationalized teachers are treated at par.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Furthermore, Rule 9(1) of the 2013 Rules provide </span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: TonnyBanglaMJ;">mivmwi wb‡qvMcÖvß me©‡kl e¨w³i wb‡¤œ D³ wkÿ‡Ki Ae¯’vb wba©vwiZ nB‡e|</span></u></strong><u> </u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;">We fail to understand the logic behind this. <u>This means that the teacher who has been nationalized, irrespective of his service as nationalized teacher, would never be senior to the direct appointees, irrespective of the date of appointment</u>. (emphasis added)</span></p><p class="Normal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">16.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;">There is an alternative interpretation of Rule 9(1) of the 2013 Rules. The interpretation is that a nationalized teacher would not be junior to the direct appointee, irrespective of the date of appointment of the latter; the nationalized teacher would be junior to the direct appointee who was appointed immediately prior to the appointment of the nationalized teacher. On the face of it, this interpretation seems sound; he who is appointed first should be senior. The problem arises because previous tenure of service in the private schools is recognized by the 2013 Rules. On the date when a nationalized teacher is appointed, he carries forward a deemed tenure of service. Under this interpretation, the deemed tenure of service recognized by first part of Rule 9(1) would cease to be recognized by the second part of Rule 9(1). The problem is illustrated by the following example. Y is a nationalized teacher with work experience of 10 years prior to his appointment under the 2013 Rules in say, 2014. His deemed length of service in 2014 i.e. on the date of his appointment, would be 5 years. Z is a direct appointee. Z is appointed immediately before Y. Z’s appointment is in 2013, exactly one year before Y’s appointment. In 2014, on the date of Y’s appointment, Z’s tenure of service would be 1 year. However, because of Rule 9(1) of the 2013 Rules, Y will be deemed to have been in service for 5 years and yet, Y will be regarded as junior to Z because of the following </span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: TonnyBanglaMJ;">“<strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">D³ Zvwi‡Li Ae¨ewnZ c~‡e© wb‡qvMwewai Aaxb wkÿK c‡` mivmwi wb‡qvMcÖvß me©‡kl e¨w³i wb‡¤œ D³ wkÿ‡Ki Ae¯’vb wba©vwiZ nB‡e|</strong></span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;"> The quoted part of Rule 9(1) of the 2013 Rules, in our view, renders the first part of the Rule 9(1) being “</span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: TonnyBanglaMJ;">wkÿ‡Ki wb‡qvM cÖ`v‡bi ZvwiL nB‡Z Kvh©KiPvKzix Kv‡ji wfwË‡Z wkÿK c‡` Zvnvi †R¨ôZv MYbv Kiv nB‡e</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: TonnyBanglaMJ;">”</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman',serif;"> , redundant. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">17.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">It appears that the teachers who are nationalized are affected because their seniority would not be properly recognized. This is irrespective of how we interpret Rule 9(10 of the 2013 Rules. This in turn would affect their </span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: TonnyBanglaMJ;">c‡`vbœwZ, wm‡jKkb †MÖW Ges cÖ‡hvR¨ UvBg †¯‹j</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> because under Rule 9(3) of the 2013 Rules </span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: TonnyBanglaMJ;">wb‡qvM wewai kZ© c~iY mv‡c‡ÿ, Dc-wewa (1) I (2) Gi Aaxb <u>†R¨ôZvi wfwË‡Z wkÿKMY c‡`vbœwZ, wm‡jKkb †MÖW Ges cÖ‡hvR¨ UvBg †¯‹j cÖvc¨ nB‡eb</u></span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ;">|</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> (emphasis added)</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: -9.0pt 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">18.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">We have carefully reviewed the Affidavit in Oppositions filed. Though the legality of Rule 9 was challenged, the respondents did not provide any cogent justification as to why we should not interfere. The respondents also did not set out the rationale behind Rule 9(1) of the 2013 Rules. Even when we pointed out that Rule 9(1) is manifestly absurd for the reasons we have set out aforesaid, the learned Counsels for the respondents could not provide any interpretation, alternative to our interpretations. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: -9.0pt 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">19.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The learned Counsels pointed out that the 2013 Rules was duly framed under Primary Schools (Taking Over) Act 1974. This is neither here nor there. The executives were empowered by the Primary Schools (Taking Over) Act 1974 to frame Rules and in exercise of the powers so conferred, the respondents framed the 2013 Rules. In the instant case, we are not dealing with any issue relating <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">to procedural irregularity/illegality committed</span> at the time of framing of the 2013 Rules. We are dealing with the issue whether Rule 9(1) and Rule 2(Ga) of the 2013 Rules <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">should be struck down as being unreasonable. </span>We have concluded that Rule 9(1) of the 2013 Rules is manifestly unreasonable and self contradictory and therefore, is liable to be struck down.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: -9.0pt 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">20.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Before we part with the judgment, we would wish to address three more issues. First, the learned Counsels for the respondents submit that the petitioners are not qualified. However, no documents are annexed in support of the contentions. Even assuming they are not qualified, the 2013 Rules permit the petitioners to gain the requisite qualifications.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Rule 4 (1)(kha) reads as follows: </span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: TonnyBanglaMJ;">†Kvb wkÿ‡Ki `dv (K) †Z DwjøwLZ Ab¨vb¨ †hvM¨Zv _vKv m‡Ë¡I †Kej cÖ‡qvRbxq †hvM¨Zv bv _vwK‡j, AvB‡bi </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: TonnyBanglaMJ;">Section 3<strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"> Gi</strong> </span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Sub Section (1) </span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: TonnyBanglaMJ;">Gi Aaxb AwaMÖnYK…Z mswkøó we`¨vj‡qi AwaMÖn‡Yi ZvwiL nB‡Z cieZ©x 3 (wZb) erm‡ii g‡a¨ D³ †hvM¨Zv AR©‡bi k‡Z© wb‡qvM cÖ`vb Kwiqv cÖ‡qvRbxq Av‡`k Rvwi Kwi‡e|</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> In the context of Rule 4(1) (kha), </span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: TonnyBanglaMJ;">cÖ‡qvRbxq †hvM¨Zv</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> means educational qualification [ Rule 2 (cha)].</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: -9.0pt 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">21.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Secondly, the learned Counsels for the respondents submit that the petitioners preferred series of writ petitions on the same issue. We have reviewed the judgments passed in those writ petitions. The issues raised in those writ petitions are not the same as those raised in the instant writ petition. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: -9.0pt 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">22.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Thirdly, the learned Counsels submit that the Rule is not maintainable since the petitioners, as Government employees, should have subjected themselves to the jurisdiction of Administrative Tribunal. This argument is devoid of any merit. The petitioners have, in the instant writ petition, challenged among others, the legality of Rule 2(Ga) and Rule 9 (1) of the 2013. This is not a matter for Administrative Tribunal.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: -9.0pt 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">23.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In view of the above, we are inclined to hold that there is merit in the Rule.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>The Rule is made absolute in part. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: -9.0pt 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">24.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">It is declared that:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .75in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(i)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">     </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Rule 2(Ga)<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>of the 2013 Rule is not illegal; and</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo1; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .75in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(ii)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">   </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">The following in Rule 9(1), being </span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: TonnyBanglaMJ;">Ges D³ Zvwi‡Li Ae¨ewnZ c~‡e© wb‡qvMwewai Aaxb wkÿK c‡` mivmwi wb‡qvMcÖvß me©‡kl e¨w³i wb‡¤œ D³ wkÿ‡Ki Ae¯’vb wba©vwiZ nB‡e</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> is illegal and without lawful authority.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">25.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In light of the above, the respondents directed to confer seniority to the petitioners and henceforth determine the seniority and benefits payable to them by reference to </span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: TonnyBanglaMJ;">ÒKvh©Ki PvKzixKvjÓ</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> as defined in Rule 2 (Ga) of the 2013 Rules. With respect to those petitioners who are Headmasters, the respondents are further directed to treat them and not the junior direct appointees as Headmasters and publish appropriate orders(s) if necessary, through official gazette.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">26.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Communicate the Judgment and Order at once for immediate compliance.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Ed. </span></strong></p><div style="mso-element: footnote-list;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><!--[endif]--><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal"><a href="file:///H:/Issue_%20October%202019%20(2)/Issue%20__October__19(2)__W.%20P.%2014344%20of%2017_Naima%20Haider,%20J.__2.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt;">Writ Petition No. 14344 of 2017</span></strong></a></p></div></div></div></div>

There is nothing on record to show that in approaching the wrong forum there was any <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">bona fide</em> of the learned lawyer or the petitioners themselves. There is also noting to hold such a view that there was due diligence and caution from the side of the petitioners before moving the wrong forum<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>under the ambit of<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>relevant law. In case of such inordinate delay it is a decided matter in our arena that the delay of each </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">and every day must be explained satisfactorily</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> from the expiry of the date<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>of limitation up to the date of institution. The party concern can prove that they were due diligent and <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">bona fide </em><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span>and were prevented by sufficient cause from bringing the case within time, the delay can be condoned. <span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                                </span>. . . (9 and 10)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">No one appears, Advocate</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">. . .For the petitioners</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr. S. N. Goshawmi, Advocate</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">. . .For the opposite parties</span></em></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Soumendra Sarker, J. </span></u></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The Rule was issued calling upon the opposite parties to show cause as to why the delay of 3343 days in filing the revisional application against the judgment and decree dated 24.10.1992 passed by the learned the then Subordinate Judge, Pabna in Other class Suit No. 73 of 1980 affirming those dated 29.02.1980 passed by the learned the then Munsif, 3<sup>rd</sup> Court, Pabna in Other Class Suit No. 23 of 1970 should not be condoned and/or pass such other or further order or orders as to this Court may seem fit and proper.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The facts giving rise to the issuance of the Rule in a nutshell can be stated thus: The present opposite parties as plaintiffs instituted the original suit for declaration of title in the court of the then Munsif, 3<sup>rd</sup> Court, Pabna being Other Class Suit No. 23 of 1997 against the defendant-petitioner-applicants. After trial the suit was decreed on contest on 29.02.1980.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Being aggrieved the defendants preferred an appeal being Other Class Appeal No. 73 of 1980 in the court of the learned District Judge, Pabna which was transmitted to the court of learned subordinate Judge, Pabna for hearing and disposal and the learned appellate court on hearing the appeal disallowed the same and affirmed the judgment and decree passed by the learned trial court on 24.10.1992.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Being aggrieved by and dissatisfied with the impugned judgment and decree, the defendant-petitioner-applicants preferred a revisional application under Section 115(1) of the Code of Civil Procedure, before this court, but in filing of the revisional application there has been a delay of 3343 days.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">For condonation of the said delay the defendant-petitioners have filed an application under section 05 read with Section 14 of the Limitation Act contending <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">inter alia </em>that the defendant-applicants being dissatisfied with the judgment and decree passed by the learned Appellate Court in Other Class Appeal No. 73 of 1980 filed a review application under Order XLVII Rule 1 of the Code of Civil Procedure and the application for review was heard and disposed of on 12.11.2001. The application for review since was dismissed the defendants felt aggrieved and have preferred the revisional application before this court. The further case of the defendant-applicants is such that in wrong forum the review application was preferred against the judgment and decree passed by the appellate court and for that reason the delay occurred which is unintentional and <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">bona fide. </em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">On the said application, a Rule was issued and during hearing of the Rule Mr. S. N. Goswami the learned Advocate appeared on behalf of the opposite parties but none appeared on behalf of the petitioners, despite; the matter was posted in the delay cause list of this Bench with the name of the learned Advocate for the petitioners for days together.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 107%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 107%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 107%; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">The grounds as alleged within the contents</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 107%;"> of the application for condonation of delay is such that the proceedings of the case was in wrong forum and due to wrong forum since the delay occurred, the petitioners have prayed for condonation of delay which is 3343 days. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">As against the grounds of the application for condonation of delay, the learned Advocate appearing on behalf of the opposite parties after referring two decisions of this court<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>reported in 24 BLT 240 and 25 BLT 29<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>controverting the grounds of the application for condonation of delay submits that the provisions laid down in section 05 read with section 14 of the Limitation Act cannot be invoked in the instant case inasmuch as<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>from the facts and circumstances of the case it appears from the face of the record that the original Other Class Suit No. 23 of 1970 and the subsequent appeal which was filed by the present petitioners were disposed of on contest. On 24.10.1992 the judgment and decree was passed in Other Appeal No. 73 of 1980 which was well within the knowledge of the petitioners and the petitioners showing gross negligence and not in clean hands instead of filing of the revisional application deliberately after an inordinate delay of 3343 days, have filed the revisional application and there is no scope to hold such a view that for <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">bona fide </em><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span>reason the delay occurred. The learned Advocate<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>further submits that there is no satisfactory explanation from the side of the petitioners as to why the unusual delay of 3343 days occurred and it is a decided matter in our judicature that inasmuch as from the conduct of the petitioners it is apparent that they have preferred a review application before the appellate court after disposal of the appeal which is admittedly the wrong forum and that was chosen by the defendant-petitioner-applicants themselves, it cannot be treated sufficient cause within the meaning of section 05 of the Limitation Act. This Bench in the case of Ms. Ok-Kyung Oh vs. Tea Hung Packaging<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>(Bd.) Ltd. and others, 24 BLT 240 held :</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">            </span>“ the conduct of the petitioner herself in choosing wrong forum cannot be treated ‘sufficient cause’ within the meaning<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>of<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>section 5 of the Limitation Act. Besides this; the ground of the application for condonation of delay as it appears is not proper to hold such a view that the mistake done by the plaintiff-appellant-petitioner was bonafide and she was diligent in filing the civil revision within time. Cause of delay as cited within the contents of the application under section 5 of the Limitation Act (IX of 1908) appears to be evasive and it is no doubt that only due to self-impression of the petitioner this delay of 2091 days occurred; which is not at all satisfactory. Moreover; it is settled that in the application filed under section 5 of the Limitation Act the petitioner is required to explain each day’s delay to the satisfaction of the Court.” </span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In order to appreciate the submission advanced from the side of the learned counsel for the opposite parties, on perusal of the grounds of the application for condonation of delay filed under section 05 read with section 14 of the Limitation Act, 1908 it is obvious to note that the explanation given<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>from the side of the petitioner-applicants is not at all satisfactory and it cannot be treated as <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">bona fide </em>for condonation of the said inordinate delay of 3343 days. Apart from this, admittedly the review application was dismissed on 12.11.2001 but the revisional application has been filed on 30.03.2002 and there is no explanation as to why this delay was caused, when 12.11.2001 was within the knowledge of the petitioners. Furthermore, it is apparent from the face of the records that in between the dates as cited within the contents of the application, there exist no reasonable link. There is nothing on record to show that in approaching the wrong forum there was any <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">bona fide</em> of the learned lawyer or the petitioners themselves. There is also noting to hold such a view that there was due diligence and caution from the side of the petitioners before moving the wrong forum<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>under the ambit of<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>relevant law. In case of such inordinate delay it is a decided matter in our arena that the delay of each and every day must be explained satisfactorily from the expiry of the date<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>of limitation up to the date of institution [Ref. 5 DLR 20; 25 DLR 254 ].</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Furthermore, within the ambit of section 05 read with section 14 of the Limitation Act, 1908 where the party concern can prove that they were due diligent and <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">bona fide </em><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span>and were prevented by sufficient cause from bringing the case within time, the delay can be condoned. But in the instant case<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>as I have come across that the petitioner-applicants are not at all diligent or <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">bona fide </em>in filing the revisional application within time, rather; they were very much negligent, dormant and callous in filing the case within time and law does not permit the court to help any<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>such dormant. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">11.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Having regard to the facts, circumstances and the discussions referred to above, I am constrained to hold such a view that the argument advanced from the side of the learned counsel Mr. S. N. Goshawmi is well founded and hence, the Rule has got no substance to succeed. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">12.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In the result; the Rule is discharged without any order as to costs.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Ed. </span></strong></p><div style="mso-element: footnote-list;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><!--[endif]--><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal"><a href="file:///H:/Issue_%20October%202019%20(2)/Issue%20__October__19(2)__C.%20Rule%20_114(con)%20of%2002_Soumendra%20Sarker,%20J.__1.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt;">Civil Rule No. 114 (con) of 2002</span></strong></a></p></div></div></div></div>
806	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">National Bank Ltd Vs. M. R. Trading Company</h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> CIVIL PETITION FOR LEAVE TO APPEAL No. 3970 OF 2018. </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  Hasan Foez Siddique, J.)</p><p><b>Court:</b> Appellate Division ,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. Rokanuddin Mahmud, Senior Advocate, instructed by Mr. Zainul Abedin, Advocate-on-Record.,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2019(2) LNJ (AD) </p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2019</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  National Bank Limited and another </p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  M. R. Trading Company, represented by Alhaj Md. Mizanur Rahman and others  </p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Artha Rin Adalat Ain </p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2020-03-15</p><!DOCTYPE html><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;
